       4             : /*
       5             :  * This file implements PKCS 11 on top of our existing security modules
       6             :  *
       7             :  * For more information about PKCS 11 See PKCS 11 Token Inteface Standard.
       8             :  *   This implementation has two slots:
       9             :  *      slot 1 is our generic crypto support. It does not require login.
      10             :  *   It supports Public Key ops, and all they bulk ciphers and hashes.
      11             :  *   It can also support Private Key ops for imported Private keys. It does
      12             :  *   not have any token storage.
      13             :  *      slot 2 is our private key support. It requires a login before use. It
      14             :  *   can store Private Keys and Certs as token objects. Currently only private
      15             :  *   keys and their associated Certificates are saved on the token.
      16             :  *
      17             :  *   In this implementation, session objects are only visible to the session
      18             :  *   that created or generated them.
      19             :  */

    2456             : 
    2457             : /* NSC_SignInit setups up the signing operations. There are three basic
    2458             :  * types of signing:
    2459             :  *      (1) the tradition single part, where "Raw RSA" or "Raw DSA" is applied
    2460             :  *  to data in a single Sign operation (which often looks a lot like an
    2461             :  *  encrypt, with data coming in and data going out).
    2462             :  *      (2) Hash based signing, where we continually hash the data, then apply
    2463             :  *  some sort of signature to the end.
    2464             :  *      (3) Block Encryption CBC MAC's, where the Data is encrypted with a key,
    2465             :  *  and only the final block is part of the mac.
    2466             :  *
    2467             :  *  For case number 3, we initialize a context much like the Encryption Context
    2468             :  *  (in fact we share code). We detect case 3 in C_SignUpdate, C_Sign, and
    2469             :  *  C_Final by the following method... if it's not multi-part, and it's doesn't
    2470             :  *  have a hash context, it must be a block Encryption CBC MAC.
    2471             :  *
    2472             :  *  For case number 2, we initialize a hash structure, as well as make it
    2473             :  *  multi-part. Updates are simple calls to the hash update function. Final
    2474             :  *  calls the hashend, then passes the result to the 'update' function (which
    2475             :  *  operates as a final signature function). In some hash based MAC'ing (as
    2476             :  *  opposed to hash base signatures), the update function is can be simply a
    2477             :  *  copy (as is the case with HMAC).
    2478             :  */
